(TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [In the vulgar modern language, it means <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a horse or the like) <hi rend="ital">galloped.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence,] said of the [locust termed] <foreign lang="ar">جُنْدَب</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It struck the pebbles:</hi> (so in three copies of the S:) or <hi rend="ital">it struck the pebbles with its hind leg,</hi> (L and A, and so, accord. to the TA, in the S,) or <hi rend="ital">with its two hind legs.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And, said of lightning, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It gleamed</hi> (A, K) <hi rend="ital">with gleams slight and near together.</hi> (A.)    </entryFree>26:T23b1,<entryFree id="n16599" key="رُمْحٌ" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">A certain weapon,</hi> (L, TA,) <hi rend="ital">well known;</hi> (L, Msb, K;) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">a spear,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lance; one with which one thrusts, not which one casts;</hi> accord. to El-Hareeree, (cited by De Sacy in his “ Chrest. (L.) [Hence the saying,] <foreign lang="ar">كَسَرُوا بَيْنَهُمْ رُمْحًا</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">They broke a spear between them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">among them;</hi> meaning] <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">evil,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mischief,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">enmity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">contention,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">happened between them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">among them.</hi> (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">مُنِينَا بِيَوْمٍ كَظِلِّ الرُّمْحِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">We were tried with a long and distressing day.</hi> (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">هُمْ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَنِى فُلَانٍ رُمْحٌ وَاحِدٌ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">They are in league against the sons of such a one as one man</hi>]. (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّ عَيْنَيْهِ فِى رُمْحَيْنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">As though his two eyes were upon two spears</hi>] is said of one in fear and fright, and looking hardly, or intently; and sometimes of one in anger. (TA.) [The dim. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n16599-1" target="رُمَيْحٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n16603"/></foreign>. And hence the saying,] <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَ رُمَيْحَ أَبِى</foreign>

(K, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">رَامِحٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [As a measure in astronomy, accord. to modern Arabian astronomers, it is <hi rend="ital">Four degrees and a half;</hi> the <hi rend="ital">eightieth part of a great circle;</hi> and accord. to various works on practical law, it consists of <hi rend="ital">twelve</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَشْبَار</foreign> (or <hi rend="ital">spans</hi>): but there is reason to believe that ancient usage differed from the modern, with respect to both these measures, and was not precise nor uniform: in an instance mentioned voce <foreign lang="ar">زُبَانَى</foreign>, it appears to be about twice the measure stated above; i. e., about <hi rend="ital">nine degrees;</hi> and to consist of <hi rend="ital">five cubits,</hi> a measure perhaps equal to <hi rend="ital">twelve spans.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَتْ رِمَاحَهَا</foreign>, said of the [species of barley-grass called] <foreign lang="ar">بُهْمَى</foreign>, (T, S, A, TA,) and of any similar pasture, (T, TA,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">It assumed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">put forth, its prickles,</hi> (A, * TA,) or <hi rend="ital">became dry in its prickles,</hi> (T, TA,) <hi rend="ital">and thus</hi> (T, A, TA) <hi rend="ital">resisted the attempts of animals to pasture upon it.</hi> (T, S, A, L, TA.) (TA.) One says also <foreign lang="ar">نَاقَةٌ ذَاتُ رُمْحٍ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A fat she-camel;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">إِبِلٌ ذَوَاتُ رِمَاحٍ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">fat camels;</hi> because their owner, when desiring to slaughter them, looks at their fatness and their goodly appearance, and is prevented from slaughtering them.
